Erroneous Solutions of the Karamiyya and Mu'tazila
The author identifies the source of error and describes two heretical views on divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Karamiyya and Mu'tazila erroneously attempted to explain the specification of the world through divine will, and the key differences between their positions.

Core Idea
Both sects introduce temporality into God's relation to the world, but in opposing ways.

The author begins by pointing to a pivotal source of theological error. He then contrasts two misguided solutions: the Karamiyya placed temporal events in God's essence, while the Mu'tazila posited temporal wills with no spatial location. Understanding these views clarifies why they are rejected in orthodox Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage aloud
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Let the original wording sink in before analyzing.
Notice the parallel structure describing each sect.
2
Identify the two sects
Locate where the text mentions the Karamiyya and the Mu'tazila. Write down their core claims in your own words.
The Karamiyya are described first, then the Mu'tazila.
3
Examine the distinctions made by the Karamiyya
The Karamiyya differentiate between eternal intention and temporal will, and between events and the creator of events. Consider why they made these distinctions.
They try to preserve God's transcendence while explaining particularization.
4
Contrast with the Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila affirm temporal wills but not in a locus, and they do not make the distinctions the Karamiyya made. Reflect on the implications.
Both views are rejected for introducing temporality in different ways.
5
Reflect on the author's assessment
Why does the author call this point a 'source of error'? Consider how both positions fall short of the orthodox understanding of God's will.
The correct view affirms an eternal will without temporal events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الموضع منشأ ضلال بعض المتكلمين، فإن الكرامية أثبتوا حوادث في ذات الباري تعالى من الإرادة والقول، وهي التي تخصص العالم بالوجود دون العدم، والمشية القديمة تتعلق عندهم تعلقا عاماً، والإرادة تتعلق تعلقا خاصا، وفرقوا بين الأحداث والمحدث والخلق والمخلوق، والمعتزلة أثبتوا إرادات حادثة لا في محل هي التي تخصص العالم بالوجود دون العدم، ولم يفرقوا بين الأحداث والمحدث والخلق والمخلوق.
And this point is the source of the error of some theologians. For the Karamiyya asserted temporal events (ḥawādith) in the essence of the Most High God, from will and speech, which are what specify the world to existence rather than non-existence. In their view, the eternal intention (al-mashiyya al-qadīma) is general in attachment, while will (al-irāda) is specific in attachment. They distinguished between temporal events (al-aḥdāth) and the creator of events (al-muḥdith), and between creation (al-khalq) and the created (al-makhlūq). The Mu'tazila asserted temporal wills (irādāt ḥāditha) not in a locus, which specify the world to existence rather than non-existence, and they did not distinguish between temporal events and the creator of events, nor between creation and the created.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage classifies two erroneous theological schools concerning the divine will that specifies the world. The Karamiyya held that events (ḥawādith) — specifically temporal volitions and speech — occur in God's essence as a means of particularization. They distinguished the eternal intention (general) from temporal will (specific), and also made a terminological distinction between 'events' (aḥdāth) and the 'maker of events' (muḥdith), and between 'creation' (khalq) and 'the created' (makhlūq). The Mu'tazila, in contrast, affirmed temporal wills but not located in any subject (lā fī maḥall), and they did not make these distinctions. The author implies that both positions are mistaken because they introduce temporality into God or bypass the problem of specification without a sound basis.

Key Terms
الكرامية
المعتزلة
الحوادث
المشية القديمة
الإرادة
الأحداث
المحدث
الخلق
المخلوق
الإرادات الحادثة لا في محل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Mu'tazila also believed temporal events occur in God's essence, since they affirm temporal wills.
Correction: The Mu'tazila specifically denied a locus for those wills; they are not in God's essence nor anywhere else.

Checkpoint
How did the Karamiyya differ from the Mu'tazila regarding divine will?
A) The Karamiyya denied temporal wills, while the Mu'tazila affirmed them.
B) The Karamiyya asserted temporal events in God's essence, while the Mu'tazila posited temporal wills not in a locus.
C) The Karamiyya and Mu'tazila held identical views.
D) The Karamiyya affirmed temporal wills not in a locus, while the Mu'tazila affirmed them in God's essence.

Key Takeaway
The erroneous views of the Karamiyya and Mu'tazila both introduce temporality into the divine, but they differ in whether they place temporal wills in God's essence or nowhere.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking that God's will changes or adapts to new circumstances? How does this passage's warning against introducing temporality into God challenge that subtle assumption, and what concrete step will you take today to internalize that God's will is eternal and unchanging?
?
The Karamiyya and Mu'tazila both relied on their reasoning and fell into error. In what area of your own understanding of Allah might your logic be leading you away from the revelation? Pause and ask yourself: is there any belief you hold about God that is not directly from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and if so, are you willing to abandon it?
?
This passage calls out the error of placing temporal events in God's essence. How does this affect the way you speak about Allah and His attributes? Will you commit to using only the terms and descriptions that Allah has used for Himself, leaving aside speculative elaborations? Write one practical change you will make in your daily conversations or thoughts about God.

Disagreement Among Philosophers on the Order of Emanation
Points out internal disagreements among philosophers about the order of emanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the philosophers themselves disagreed on the order of first principles in their emanation scheme, revealing the weakness of their doctrine.

Core Idea
Philosophers cannot agree on the first principle—a clear sign their doctrine is uncertain.

Having outlined the philosophers' emanation scheme in general, the author now points out a crucial flaw: the philosophers themselves disagree on the order of the principles. This internal inconsistency undermines the certainty of their claims. We will read the passage and see the two variant sequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to familiarize yourself with the two orders.
2
Identify the two orders
Write down the two sequences given. Notice which principles are placed first in each.
The first sequence begins with 'element' (perhaps prime matter?), the second with 'intellect'.
3
Understand the implication
Reflect on why this disagreement matters: if the philosophers cannot agree, their system is not based on certainty.
The author uses this as an argument against the philosophers' authority.
4
Consider the significance
Think about how this internal dispute relates to the broader theological argument of the book.
Later, the author will refute these views based on revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هم منازعون في الترتيب الذي ذكروه، فإن أصحابهم قد اختلفوا في المبادي اختلافًا ظاهراً؛ فمنهم من قال: أول الموجودات هو العنصر ثم العقل ثم النفس ثم الجسم، ومنهم من قال: العقل ثم النفس ثم الهيولي ثم الأفلاك ثم العناصر ثم المركبات، كما سيأتي بيان ذلك.
Then they are in dispute regarding the order they mentioned. For their proponents have differed in the principles with an apparent difference. Some of them say: The first of existents is the element, then the intellect, then the soul, then the body. And some say: The intellect, then the soul, then matter, then the spheres, then the elements, then the compounds. As will be explained later.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an argument from internal disagreement: the philosophers themselves cannot agree on the order of the first principles in their emanation scheme. The author cites two variant orders: one group holds that the first existent is the element (perhaps meaning the first matter?), then intellect, then soul, then body. Another group orders it as intellect, then soul, then matter (hyle), then the spheres, then the elements, then compounds. This disagreement, the author implies, shows that the philosophers' doctrine is not a certain truth but a matter of opinion, further weakening its claim.

Key Terms
منازعون
المبادي
العنصر
الهيولي
الأفلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Philosophers all agreed on the order of emanation.
Correction: The text shows they disagreed, with some placing element first and others intellect first.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the philosophers regarding the order of emanation?
A) They all agree
B) They dispute it, with some making the element first, others the intellect first
C) They have a single established order
D) They do not discuss it

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' internal disagreement on the first principles proves their emanation doctrine is not a certain truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter disagreements among scholars on foundational issues, do you dismiss their entire field as unreliable, or do you investigate further? How does this passage affect your trust in philosophical arguments for faith?
?
This passage shows that even the greatest thinkers disagreed on the first principle. In your own life, what 'first principles' do you hold without question? Are they based on certainty or assumption?
?
How does knowing that the philosophers' system has this internal inconsistency affect your reliance on rational proofs for faith? Are you willing to accept that some truths can only be known through revelation?

Ancient Philosophers on Creation
Author lists ancient materialist theories on the first principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the variety of ancient Greek materialist views on the first principle of creation and why they are considered erroneous.

Core Idea
Ancient philosophers wrongly proposed multiple first principles instead of one Creator.

The author begins by referencing the ancient philosophers (pre-Socratics) who speculated about the origin of the universe. They allowed multiple emanations from the Necessary Existent and proposed different first principles. This lesson summarizes their diverse views to highlight their departure from monotheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on ancient philosophers
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the list of proposed first principles: water, fire, air, subtle bodies, atoms, number, love, etc.
The author mentions he has detailed these in his work al-Irshad.
2
Identify the core error
These philosophers assumed that something multiple could emanate from the Necessary Existent, implying a limitation on divine unity.
3
Reflect on the implication
Think why the author includes these views: to show that correct belief requires affirming God alone as creator without intermediaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قدماء الأوائل من جوز صدور شيء متكثر من واجب الوجود واختلفوا فيه فمنهم من قال هو الماء ومنهم من قال هو النار ومنهم من قال الهواء ومنهم من قال هو أجسام لطيفة بسيطة تركبت أو أجزاء صغار اجتمعت فحدث العالم ومنهم من قال هو العدة ومنهم من قال هو المحبة والغلبة على ما قررنا تفصيل مذاهبهم في الإرشاد إلى عقائد العباد. وأما المجوس فلهم تفصيل مذهب في حدوث الكائنات وسبب امتزاج النور والظلمة وسبب الخلاص لكن اتفقوا على نسبة الخير والصلاح إلى النور ونسبة الشر والفساد إلى الظلمة. وأما المعتزلة القدرية فأثبتوا للقدرة الحادثة تأثيرا في الإيجاد والأحداث من الحركات والسكنات وبعض الاعتقادات والاعتمادات والنظر والاستدلال والعلم الحاصل به وبعض الإدراكات وهي التي يجد الإنسان من نفسه أنها تتوقف على البواعث والدواعي وورود التكليف بمباشرتها والكف عنها.
And among the ancient ones were those who allowed the emanation of something multiple from the Necessary Existent, and they differed about it: some said it is water, some said it is fire, some said it is air, some said it is subtle simple bodies that combined, or small parts that gathered so the world came to be, some said it is number, some said it is love and dominance according to what we have detailed about their doctrines in al-Irshad to the beliefs of the servants. As for the Magians, they have a detailed doctrine on the occurrence of beings, the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and the cause of salvation, but they agreed on attributing good and righteousness to light, and evil and corruption to darkness. As for the Qadari Mu'tazila, they affirmed for temporal power an effect in causing and bringing about movements and rest, and some beliefs and intentions, and reflection and inference, and the knowledge obtained thereby, and some perceptions, and these are things that man finds from himself that they depend on motives and incentives, and the arrival of obligation to do them or abstain from them.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents three additional erroneous views on creation. First, the ancient philosophers (pre-Socratics) who allowed multiple emanations from the Necessary Existent and proposed various first principles such as water, fire, air, atoms, number, or love. The author notes he has detailed these in his other work al-Irshad. Second, the Magians (dualists) who attribute good to light and evil to darkness, with a detailed theory about the mixing and eventual salvation. Third, the Mu'tazila (Qadariyya) who affirm that temporal human power has a real effect in causing actions like movements, beliefs, and reasoning, and that these depend on motives and divine obligation. The author groups these to show the range of incorrect positions that deviate from the correct belief that God alone is the true creator.

Key Terms
قدماء الأوائل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the ancient philosophers allow?
A) The world is eternal.
B) Emanation of something multiple from the Necessary Existent.
C) God is light.
D) Human power creates actions.

Key Takeaway
The ancient philosophers erred by proposing multiple first principles, undermining the oneness of the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you explain the world around you—your health, your success, your safety—do you ever unconsciously attribute it to natural causes like 'luck' or 'hard work' without immediately remembering that Allah alone is the Creator and Sustainer? What would it take for you to mentally pause and redirect that credit to Him every time?
?
The ancient philosophers allowed multiple origins for the universe. In your own heart, do you sometimes rely on multiple 'sources' for your well-being: your job, your family, your skills? Are you willing to identify one such false prop and cut it off, entrusting your affairs solely to Allah?
?
This passage seems like ancient history. But consider: the modern world also proposes multiple first principles—science, evolution, chance. Do you ever catch yourself thinking that Allah created through these means in a way that diminishes His direct power? What change in your daily thinking would this lesson demand of you?

Magian Dualism on Creation
Author summarizes the dualistic doctrine of the Magians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Magian dualistic doctrine of light and darkness and why it is considered a false belief about creation.

Core Idea
Magians wrongly attribute good to light and evil to darkness as independent principles.

Next, the author turns to the Magians (Zoroastrians) who held a dualistic cosmology. They believed in two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Their detailed doctrine explains the mixing of these two and the eventual salvation. This lesson presents their view and its error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Magians
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the Magians have a detailed theory about the occurrence of beings, mixing of light/darkness, and salvation.
2
Identify the key error
They attribute good to light and evil to darkness as two independent principles, denying that all good and evil are from God alone.
3
Understand the implication
This dualism compromises God's absolute power and unity, as evil would come from an independent source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قدماء الأوائل من جوز صدور شيء متكثر من واجب الوجود واختلفوا فيه فمنهم من قال هو الماء ومنهم من قال هو النار ومنهم من قال الهواء ومنهم من قال هو أجسام لطيفة بسيطة تركبت أو أجزاء صغار اجتمعت فحدث العالم ومنهم من قال هو العدة ومنهم من قال هو المحبة والغلبة على ما قررنا تفصيل مذاهبهم في الإرشاد إلى عقائد العباد. وأما المجوس فلهم تفصيل مذهب في حدوث الكائنات وسبب امتزاج النور والظلمة وسبب الخلاص لكن اتفقوا على نسبة الخير والصلاح إلى النور ونسبة الشر والفساد إلى الظلمة. وأما المعتزلة القدرية فأثبتوا للقدرة الحادثة تأثيرا في الإيجاد والأحداث من الحركات والسكنات وبعض الاعتقادات والاعتمادات والنظر والاستدلال والعلم الحاصل به وبعض الإدراكات وهي التي يجد الإنسان من نفسه أنها تتوقف على البواعث والدواعي وورود التكليف بمباشرتها والكف عنها.

What do the Magians attribute to darkness according to the passage?
A) Light and good.

The Magians' dualism is false because it attributes evil to an independent principle, compromising God's absolute power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself blaming your mistakes or bad circumstances on things outside Allah's control—like 'bad luck' or other people? How does the Magians' error of attributing evil to an independent darkness mirror your own tendency to shift blame? What would change if you fully accepted that everything, good and bad, comes from Allah?
?
Reflect on a recent difficulty you faced. Did you immediately wonder 'Why did this happen to me?' as if something evil had intruded from outside? How can you retrain your heart to see that trial as a decree from Allah, with wisdom and purpose, rather than as an alien force?
?
When you experience ease and blessing, do you thank Allah, or do you sometimes feel you 'deserved' it or attribute it to your own efforts? How does the Magians' dualism tempt you to think that good comes from one source and evil from another? Commit to acknowledging Allah as the sole creator of every joy and every hardship today.

Mu'tazila on Human Power
Author summarizes the Mu'tazila doctrine on the causal efficacy of human power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila belief that human temporal power has real causal effect in creating actions, and why this is considered a doctrinal error.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila wrongly affirm that human power can create actions, diminishing divine omnipotence.

Finally, the author addresses the Qadari Mu'tazila, who overemphasized human free will. They claimed that the temporal power (qudra haditha) given to humans has a real effect in causing actions such as movements, beliefs, and reasoning. This lesson explains their view and the author's refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Mu'tazila
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the list of actions they claim human power affects: movements, rest, beliefs, intentions, reflection, inference, etc.
2
Identify the key error
They affirm that temporal power has an effect in creating (ijad and ihdath), which ascribes creative power to humans.
3
Understand why it's wrong
Creation is exclusive to God. Human power is only an acquired attribute, not creative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What do the Mu'tazila affirm for temporal power?
A) No effect at all.
B) An effect in causing and bringing about actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something through your own effort, do you ever feel a sense of pride that overlooks Allah's role as the true Creator of that action? How does this lesson's warning against attributing causal power to humans challenge you to re-examine that feeling? What specific step can you take today to consciously attribute all your successes to Allah's power alone?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that human power has an effect in bringing about actions. In your daily life, are there moments when you act as if your choices and abilities are independent of Allah's will? How can you train yourself to see your own power as merely a means that Allah creates and sustains?
?
This lesson states that the Mu'tazila's view diminishes divine omnipotence. Have you ever unwittingly diminished Allah's greatness in your heart by overestimating your own control over events? What would it look like for you to truly submit to Allah's absolute power in a situation you are currently facing?

Views on Causation and Points of Agreement
Author summarizes groups' views on the world's cause and states three points of agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing opinions among theological groups regarding the cause of the world's temporal origination and the specific points where the author agrees with each group.

Core Idea
The author finds common ground with diverse groups while maintaining that only God truly creates.

This passage presents a fascinating overview of various theological positions on causation. The author summarizes disagreements about the world's cause, then highlights specific agreements with Philosophers, Magians, and Mu'tazila. This shows his method of selective concurrence while upholding Ash'ari doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups mentioned
Read the passage and list the groups: those who say the cause is 'number/readiness' or 'love/domination', the Magians, the Mu'tazila, and the Philosophers.
The author references his earlier work for full details on the first two views.
2
Understand each group's view
Focus on the Magian dualism (light/darkness) and Mu'tazilite affirmation of human power's real effect. Note how they differ from Ash'ari position.
3
Examine the three agreements
The author states three specific points of agreement: with Philosophers on bodies not creating bodies, with Magians on darkness not caused by light, and with Mu'tazila on temporal power not creating bodies, colors, etc.
These agreements are limited negations, not endorsements of full systems.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجتمعت على حدوث العالم، ومنهم من قال: هو العدة، ومنهم من قال: هو المحبة والغلبة على ما قررنا تفصيل مذاهبهم في الإرشاد إلى عقائد العباد. وأما المجوس فلهم تفصيل مذهب في حدوث الكائنات، وسبب امتزاج النور والظلمة وسبب الخلاص، لكن اتفقوا على نسبة الخير والصلاح إلى النور، ونسبة الشر والفساد إلى الظلمة. وأما المعتزلة القدرية فأثبتوا للقدرة الحادثة تأثيرًا في الإيجاد والأحداث من الحركات والسكنات، وبعض الاعتقادات والاعتمادات والنظر والاستدلال والعلم الحاصل به وبعض الإدراكات، وهي التي يجد الإنسان من نفسه أنها تتوقف على البواعث والدواعي، وورود التكليف بمباشرتها والكف عنها. ووافقنا الفلاسفة على أن جسماً ما أو قوة في جسم لا يصلح أن يكون مبدعًا للجسم. ووافقنا المجوس على أن الظلمة لا يجوز أن تحدث بإحداث النور. ووافقنا المعتزلة على أن القدرة الحادثة لا تصلح لأحداث الأجسام والألوان والطعوم والروائح، وبعض الإدراكات والحياة والموت ولهم اختلاف مذهب في المتولدات.
They agreed on the occurrence of the world, and among them are those who said: it is the [؟] number/readiness, and among them are those who said: it is love and domination, according to what we have set forth in detail of their schools in al-Irshad ila 'Aqa'id al-'Ibad. As for the Magians, they have a detailed school concerning the occurrence of things, and the cause of the mixture of light and darkness, and the cause of deliverance, but they agreed on attributing good and righteousness to light, and attributing evil and corruption to darkness. As for the Mu'tazila Qadariyya, they affirmed for the temporal power a real effect in bringing about [؟] and producing events from movements and rest, and some beliefs and [؟] and reflection and inference and the knowledge obtained thereby, and some perceptions, which are those that a person finds from himself that they depend on motives and promptings, and the occurrence of the command to undertake them and refrain from them. And we agreed with the Philosophers that a certain body or a power in a body is not fit to be the innovator of the body. And we agreed with the Magians that darkness cannot occur by the causing of light. And we agreed with the Mu'tazila that temporal power is not fit for producing bodies, colors, tastes, smells, and some perceptions, life, and death, and they have differing schools concerning the generated things.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage classifies various groups regarding the cause of the world's creation and then states specific points of agreement. The author begins by noting that despite agreement on the world's temporal origination, groups differ on its cause: some say it is a 'number/readiness' (al-‘idda), others say 'love and domination' (al-mahabbah wa al-ghalabah). He refers to his detailed exposition in his earlier work 'al-Irshad'. Then he describes the Magians who hold that good comes from light and evil from darkness. Next, the Mu'tazila Qadariyya affirm that temporal human power has a real effect in producing actions, including movements, beliefs, and perceptions, but these depend on motives and the divine command. After describing these views, the author states three points of agreement: with the Philosophers that no body or power in a body can originate another body; with the Magians that darkness cannot be caused by light; and with the Mu'tazila that temporal power cannot produce bodies, colors, etc., though they disagree on generated effects. This shows the author's method of selective concurrence while maintaining his own position that only God creates.

Correction: He only agrees on specific negations of creaturely power, not their overall systems.

The Four Considerations of the First Intellect
The author states the philosophers' claim about the four considerations of the First Intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' doctrine of the First Intellect's four considerations and how they give rise to multiplicity in the universe.

Core Idea
The First Intellect's four considerations produce the chain of creation.

This passage presents a key Neoplatonic emanation scheme adopted by some Muslim philosophers. They argue that multiplicity arises not directly from God but through the First Intellect's self-reflections. Let's examine their precise claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the four considerations listed.
2
Identify the four considerations
Find the four i'tibarat and what each one produces.
Each consideration differs in reality.
3
Reflect on the emanation chain
Understand how the intellectuals deduce a series of intellect, soul, form, matter.
This is the philosophers' attempt to explain multiplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غيره لا من ذاته، فلم يستفد الكثرة من واجب الوجود، لعمري لما حصل العقل حصلت له اعتبارات أربعة ؛ أحدها كونه واجبًا بغيره، والثاني كونه عقلا، والثالث كونه واحدًا في ذاته، والرابع كونه ممكنا في ذاته، فأوجب من حيث هو عقل عقلا، ومن حيث هو موجود بواجب الوجود نفسا ومن حيث هو واحد صورة، ومن حيث هو مكن مادة وهذه الاعتبارات لما كانت مختلفة الحقايق أوجبت جواهر مختلفة الأنواع.
Other than it, not from its essence, so it did not derive multiplicity from the Necessary Existent. By my life, when the intellect came to be, it had four considerations: one: its being necessary through another; second: its being an intellect; third: its being one in its essence; fourth: its being possible in its essence. So from the aspect of its being an intellect, it necessitated an intellect; from the aspect of its being existent through the Necessary Existent, a soul; from the aspect of its being one, a form; and from the aspect of its being possible, matter. And since these considerations had different realities, they necessitated substances of different kinds.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' doctrine regarding the First Intellect. It begins by stating that the First Intellect does not derive multiplicity directly from the Necessary Existent. Instead, when the intellect is obtained, it has four considerations (i'tibarat) that are attributed to it: (1) its being necessary through another (i.e., its existence comes from the Necessary Existent), (2) its being an intellect, (3) its being one in essence, and (4) its being possible in essence. Each consideration gives rise to a different aspect: from its being an intellect, another intellect; from its being existent through the Necessary Existent, a soul; from its being one, a form; from its being possible, matter. Because these considerations have different realities, they produce substances of different kinds. This is a key part of the Neoplatonic emanation scheme which the author will later critique.

Key Terms
اعتبارات
عقل أول
واجب الوجود
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The four considerations are real attributes of the First Intellect.
Correction: They are merely mental considerations (i'tibarat) in the philosophers' view, not real attributes.

Checkpoint

A) Necessary through another, intellect, one in essence, possible in essence
B) Eternal, intellect, one, possible
C) Necessary, intellect, soul, matter
D) Intellect, soul, form, matter

Key Takeaway
The First Intellect's four considerations are the philosophers' mechanism to derive multiplicity from unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the First Intellect needed multiple considerations to produce multiplicity, how much more does your soul need direct divine guidance to produce true faith? Are you relying on your own mental constructs or on Allah’s words to know Him?

Objection to Arbitrary Assumptions
The author objects that the four considerations are arbitrary and lack proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author forcefully rejects the philosophers' argument as pure arbitrary assumption and demands sound proof.

Core Idea
Arbitrary assumptions without proof cannot form the basis of a sound argument.

In this passage, the author directly attacks the philosophers' use of four considerations, calling them a mere 'excuse.' He insists that a valid theological argument must be grounded in either rational proof or sensory evidence, not in arbitrary correspondences. Let's see how he forcefully rebuts their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the general sense, noting the author's strong language. Then read the translation.
The word 'tahakkum' (arbitrary assumption) is a key technical term.
2
Identify the author's main claim
The author declares the philosophers' excuse to be pure arbitrary assumption lacking proof. Note the two types of proof he mentions: rational and sensory.
3
Understand the comparison with jurists
The author compares the philosophers' argument unfavorably to analogical reasoning used by jurists, which at least has a basis in expressions.
4
See the challenge
The author demands proof of the correspondences and states the philosophers cannot provide it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انظروا بعين الاعتبار إلى هذا الاعتذار، هل هو إلا تحكم محض لم يقم عليه دليل عقلي ولا شاهد حسي، بل هو أقل رتبة من طرد الفقها أرادوا بناء أشرف كمالا على اعتبارات كلها ترجع إلى عبارات، فنطالبهم أولا بصحة هذه المناسبات، ولا يجدون إلى إثباتها سبيلا.
Look with consideration at this excuse: is it anything but pure arbitrary assumption, supported by no rational proof nor sensory evidence? Rather, it is lower in rank than the argument of the jurists who wanted to build the noblest perfection on considerations that all reduce to expressions. So we demand of them, first, the validity of these correspondences, but they find no way to prove them.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an objection (i'tirad) to the philosophers' argument. The author calls their explanation an 'excuse' (i'tidhar) and declares it to be pure arbitrary assumption (tahakkum mahd). He points out that it has no rational proof (dalil 'aqli) or sensory evidence (shahid hissi). He even says it is lower in rank than the analogical reasoning of jurists (fuqaha), who base their arguments on considerations that are mere verbal expressions. The author challenges the philosophers to prove the correspondences between the considerations and the produced substances, but they cannot.

Key Terms

اعتذار
دليل عقلي
شاهد حسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is criticizing all speculative reasoning.
Correction: The author is specifically criticizing the philosophers' ungrounded assumptions, not all rational inquiry.

Checkpoint

A) A rational proof
B) Pure arbitrary assumption
C) A sensory evidence
D) A valid analogy

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' argument fails because it relies on arbitrary correspondences without any proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Two Principles of the Magian Doctrine
Author outlines two principles of Magian doctrine.

Magian dualism collapses into two key principles: origin and end.

The Magian Dualist Framework
Author presents the two pillars of Magian doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two foundational principles of the Magian doctrine regarding light and darkness, and the logical problem that arises from their opposition.

Core Idea
Dualism fails because opposites cannot mix without a cause.

The Magians (Zoroastrians) built their cosmology on two pillars: the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and the cause of their separation. The author first outlines this framework to show the inherent contradiction in claiming that two utterly opposite principles could ever combine or separate. This lesson sets the stage for the refutations that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two pillars
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how the author states the two principles: the cause of mixing (beginning) and the cause of release (return).
The passage uses the words 'مبدأ' (beginning) and 'معاد' (return).
2
Identify the problem posed
The author asks: if light and darkness are opposites in every way, how did they mix? What necessitated their union? Then, does the mixture last forever or is there a release?
This sets up the dilemma for the Magians: both options lead to difficulties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المجوس فمذهبهم يدور على قاعدتين؛ إحداهما ذكر سبب امتزاج النور والظلمة، والثانية ذكر سبب خلاص النور من الظلمة، والأولى هي المبدأ، والثانية هي المعاد، وذلك أنه لما ألزم عليهم أن النور إذا كان ضد الظلمة جوهرا وطبعا وفعلا وحيزا وهما متنافران ذاتا وطبيعة، فكيف امتزجا؟ وما الموجب لاجتماعهما حتى حصل الامتزاج، وحصل بحصول الامتزاج صور هذا العالم؟ ثم هل يبقى هذا الامتزاج أبد الدهر ويلزم عليهم كون أجزاء النور معذبة أبد الآبدين، أو تتخلص يوماً ما فما الموجب للخلاص؟ فصار مدار المسألة معهم على تقرير هذين الركنين. قالت طائفة منهم: إن النور فكر في نفسه فكرة ردية فحدث منها الظلام متشبئا ببعض أجزاء النور، وهذا قول من قال بحدوث الظلام. فيقال لهم: إذا كان النور خيراً لا شر فيه بوجه ما، فما الموجب لحدوث الفكرة الردية؟ فإن حدثت بنفسها فهلا حدث الظلام بنفسه من غير أن ينسب إليه، وإن حدث بالنور فالنور كيف أحدث أصل الشر ومنبع الفساد؟ فإنه إن كان كل فساد في العالم إنما انتسب إلى الظلام والظلام انتسب إلى الفكرة كانت الفكرة مبدأ الشر والفساد. ومن العجب أنهم اعتذروا حتى لم ينسبوا شرا جزئيا إلى النور في الحوادث، ولزمهم أن ينسبوا كل الشر وأصل الفساد إليه. ومن قال بقدم الظلام، فالرد عليه أن العقل يقضي ضرورة أن شيئين متنافرين غاية التنافر طبعا لا يمتزجان إلا بقاسر، فإنهما لو امتزجا بذاتيهما تبطل تنافرهما بذاتيهما، وما هو متنافر ذاتا لا يجوز أن يجتمع ذاتا، فالذات الواحدة لا توجب اجتماعًا وافتراقا، وذلك يقتضي ألا يحصل وجود ما وقد حصل فهو خلف.
As for the Magians, their doctrine revolves upon two principles: one is mentioning the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and the second is mentioning the cause of the release of light from darkness. The first is the beginning, and the second is the return. That is because when it was imposed upon them that light, if it is the opposite of darkness in substance, nature, act, and locus, and they are mutually antagonistic in essence and nature, how did they mix? And what necessitated their conjunction so that mixing occurred, and with the occurrence of mixing the forms of this world came into existence? Then does this mixing remain forever, and would it be necessary upon them that parts of light be tormented forever, or do they become released at some time, then what is the cause of release? So the pivot of the issue with them became the establishment of these two pillars. A group among them said: Light thought in itself a bad thought, and from it darkness arose, clinging to some parts of light. This is the opinion of those who say that darkness is originated. It is said to them: If light is good with no evil in it in any way, what necessitated the occurrence of the bad thought? For if it occurred by itself, then why did darkness not occur by itself without being attributed to it? And if it occurred by light, then how did light originate the source of evil and the fountain of corruption? For if all corruption in the world is attributed to darkness, and darkness is attributed to the thought, then the thought is the beginning of evil and corruption. And it is astonishing that they excused themselves such that they did not attribute even partial evil to light in events, but it is necessary for them to attribute all evil and the source of corruption to it. And as for those who say that darkness is eternal, the refutation against them is that reason necessarily judges that two things extremely antagonistic by nature do not mix except by a coercer; for if they mixed by their essences, their mutual antagonism would be nullified by their essences. And what is essentially antagonistic cannot be united essentially, so one essence does not necessitate both conjunction and separation. That would entail that something would not come to be, but it has come to be, so it is a contradiction.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage refutes the Magian (Zoroastrian) dualist doctrine. The author first states that their doctrine rests on two pillars: explaining the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and explaining the cause of the release of light from darkness (i.e., the beginning and the end). The problem is posed: if light and darkness are opposites in essence, substance, nature, action, and location, how could they mix? What forced them together? After mixing, does the mixture persist forever (implying parts of light are perpetually tormented) or do they separate at some point? The author then presents two Magian views. The first view: some Magians say that light had a bad thought, and from that thought darkness arose, clinging to parts of light (this is the view that darkness is originated). The refutation: if light is entirely good and contains no evil, how could a bad thought arise from it? If the thought arose by itself, then darkness could also arise by itself without being attributed to light. If light caused the thought, then light becomes the source of all evil, which contradicts its pure goodness. Thus, the Magians end up attributing all evil to light, contrary to their intention. The second view: other Magians hold that darkness is eternal. The refutation: reason dictates that two extremely opposite things cannot mix without an external coercer. If they mixed by themselves, their essential opposition would be nullified. But an essentially opposite thing cannot be united essentially; a single essence cannot necessitate both union and separation. Therefore, if mixing occurred, it would be impossible without a coercer, but they claim it happened, which is a logical contradiction.

Key Terms
المجوس
النور
الظلمة
امتزاج
الخلاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what are the two pillars of the Magian doctrine?
A) The goodness of light and the evil of darkness
B) The cause of mixing and the cause of release
C) The eternity of light and the createdness of darkness
D) The material and spiritual aspects of light

Key Takeaway
The Magian doctrine rests on explaining both the mixture and release of light and darkness, but the very opposition of the two principles raises unsolved questions about how mixture is possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever try to combine obedience to Allah with following your desires, as if they are not opposites? What cause have you offered for that mixture, and does it stand up to the same question posed to the Magians?
?
If the Magians must explain how light and darkness came together, how do you explain the coexistence of faith and sin in your own heart? Are you content to leave that question unanswered, or will you seek a resolution today?
?
The author shows that the Magian framework leads to an unsolved dilemma. Where in your own life have you accepted a contradiction without asking for its cause? What would it take to resolve it before you meet Allah?

Refuting the Magian Views on the Origin of Darkness
Author refutes two Magian views on darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two Magian views on the origin of darkness and the logical refutations the author provides against each, exposing inconsistencies in both.

Core Idea
Both originated and eternal darkness lead to contradictions.

Having established the dualist framework, the author now examines two specific Magian explanations for how darkness came to be. One group claims darkness originated from a bad thought in light; another claims darkness is eternal. The author shows that both positions collapse under rational scrutiny. This lesson walks through these refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Magian view and its refutation
Read the segment where a group says darkness arose from a bad thought in light. Note the author's response: if light is wholly good, a bad thought cannot originate from it.
The argument highlights that attributing the bad thought to light makes light the source of all evil.
2
Read the second Magian view and its refutation
Read the part about those who say darkness is eternal. The author argues that two opposites cannot mix without an external coercer.
The reasoning is that if they mixed by themselves, their essential antagonism would be nullified.
3
Compare the two refutations
Notice that both refutations use logical consistency: the first shows that attributing evil to light contradicts its nature; the second shows that eternal opposites cannot naturally unite.
Both arguments rely on the principle of non-contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المجوس فمذهبهم يدور على قاعدتين؛ إحداهما ذكر سبب امتزاج النور والظلمة، والثانية ذكر سبب خلاص النور من الظلمة، والأولى هي المبدأ، والثانية هي المعاد، وذلك أنه لما ألزم عليهم أن النور إذا كان ضد الظلمة جوهرا وطبعا وفعلا وحيزا وهما متنافران ذاتا وطبيعة، فكيف امتزجا؟ وما الموجب لاجتماعهما حتى حصل الامتزاج، وحصل بحصول الامتزاج صور هذا العالم؟ ثم هل يبقى هذا الامتزاج أبد الدهر ويلزم عليهم كون أجزاء النور معذبة أبد الآبدين، أو تتخلص يوماً ما فما الموجب للخلاص؟ فصار مدار المسألة معهم على تقرير هذين الركنين. قالت طائفة منهم: إن النور فكر في نفسه فكرة ردية فحدث منها الظلام متشبئا ببعض أجزاء النور، وهذا قول من قال بحدوث الظلام. فيقال لهم: إذا كان النور خيراً لا شر فيه بوجه ما، فما الموجب لحدوث الفكرة الردية؟ فإن حدثت بنفسها فهلا حدث الظلام بنفسه من غير أن ينسب إليه، وإن حدث بالنور فالنور كيف أحدث أصل الشر ومنبع الفساد؟ فإنه إن كان كل فساد في العالم إنما انتسب إلى الظلام والظلام انتسب إلى الفكرة كانت الفكرة مبدأ الشر والفساد. ومن العجب أنهم اعتذروا حتى لم ينسبوا شرا جزئيا إلى النور في الحوادث، ولزمهم أن ينسبوا كل الشر وأصل الفساد إليه. ومن قال بقدم الظلام، فالرد عليه أن العقل يقضي ضرورة أن شيئين متنافرين غاية التنافر طبعا لا يمتزجان إلا بقاسر، فإنهما لو امتزجا بذاتيهما تبطل تنافرهما بذاتيهما، وما هو متنافر ذاتا لا يجوز أن يجتمع ذاتا، فالذات الواحدة لا توجب اجتماعًا وافتراقا، وذلك يقتضي ألا يحصل وجود ما وقد حصل فهو خلف.
As for the Magians, their doctrine revolves upon two principles: one is mentioning the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and the second is mentioning the cause of the release of light from darkness. The first is the beginning, and the second is the return. That is because when it was imposed upon them that light, if it is the opposite of darkness in substance, nature, act, and locus, and they are mutually antagonistic in essence and nature, how did they mix? And what necessitated their conjunction so that mixing occurred, and with the occurrence of mixing the forms of this world came into existence? Then does this mixing remain forever, and would it be necessary upon them that parts of light be tormented forever, or do they become released at some time, then what is the cause of release? So the pivot of the issue with them became the establishment of these two pillars. A group among them said: Light thought in itself a bad thought, and from it darkness arose, clinging to some parts of light. This is the opinion of those who say that darkness is originated. It is said to them: If light is good with no evil in it in any way, what necessitated the occurrence of the bad thought? For if it occurred by itself, then why did darkness not occur by itself without being attributed to it? And if it occurred by light, then how did light originate the source of evil and the fountain of corruption? For if all corruption in the world is attributed to darkness, and darkness is attributed to the thought, then the thought is the beginning of evil and corruption. And it is astonishing that they excused themselves such that they did not attribute even partial evil to light in events, but it is necessary for them to attribute all evil and the source of corruption to it. And as for those who say that darkness is eternal, the refutation against them is that reason necessarily judges that two things extremely antagonistic by nature do not mix except by a coercer; for if they mixed by their essences, their mutual antagonism would be nullified by their essences. And what is essentially antagonistic cannot be united essentially, so one essence does not necessitate both conjunction and separation. That would entail that something would not come to be, but it has come to be, so it is a contradiction.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage refutes the Magian (Zoroastrian) dualist doctrine. The author first states that their doctrine rests on two pillars: explaining the cause of the mixing of light and darkness, and explaining the cause of the release of light from darkness (i.e., the beginning and the end). The problem is posed: if light and darkness are opposites in essence, substance, nature, action, and location, how could they mix? What forced them together? After mixing, does the mixture persist forever (implying parts of light are perpetually tormented) or do they separate at some point? The author then presents two Magian views. The first view: some Magians say that light had a bad thought, and from that thought darkness arose, clinging to parts of light (this is the view that darkness is originated). The refutation: if light is entirely good and contains no evil, how could a bad thought arise from it? If the thought arose by itself, then darkness could also arise by itself without being attributed to light. If light caused the thought, then light becomes the source of all evil, which contradicts its pure goodness. Thus, the Magians end up attributing all evil to light, contrary to their intention. The second view: other Magians hold that darkness is eternal. The refutation: reason dictates that two extremely opposite things cannot mix without an external coercer. If they mixed by themselves, their essential opposition would be nullified. But an essentially opposite thing cannot be united essentially; a single essence cannot necessitate both union and separation. Therefore, if mixing occurred, it would be impossible without a coercer, but they claim it happened, which is a logical contradiction.

Key Terms
فكرة ردية
قدم الظلام
امتزاج
قاسر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The refutation merely rejects dualism on religious grounds.
Correction: The author uses logical reasoning to show internal contradictions in both Magian positions, demonstrating that dualism is rationally untenable.

Checkpoint
What is the key logical problem with the view that darkness arose from a bad thought in light?
A) Light cannot think
B) If light is wholly good, it cannot be the source of a bad thought
C) The thought was actually good
D) Darkness is not real

Key Takeaway
The author uses logical reasoning to expose that both the originated and eternal darkness views lead to contradictions, thereby undermining the dualist system.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face evil or suffering, do you ever subconsciously treat it as a force co-eternal with good, as if they are equally powerful? How does this passage's logical refutation of dualism challenge your inner assumptions? What would it mean for you to truly believe that evil has no independent origin, and how should that change your response to trials?
?
Have you ever excused a small evil in yourself by attributing it to an external source, just as the Magians tried to avoid attributing evil to light? In what area of your life are you currently shifting blame for a moral failing? What would it take for you to own that failure and turn back to the One who is pure good?
?
The author says reason judges that opposites do not mix without a coercer. In your own heart, you experience conflicting desires—good and evil. Do you allow a higher authority (God's command) to coerce them into harmony, or do you let them mix on your own terms? What would change if you submitted fully to that coercer?

The Problem of Mixing Opposites and the Two Pillars
Author poses the problem of mixing two opposites and frames the debate around two pillars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Dualist position on the mixture of light and darkness and why the discussion pivots on two key pillars regarding the origin of darkness.

Core Idea
The mixing of light and darkness raises impossible questions that expose the Dualist error.

This passage invites us into the heart of the Manichaean worldview, where the world is a mixture of eternal light and eternal darkness. The author immediately identifies a fatal flaw: if they are opposites, how can they mix? He then poses two critical questions that follow from their claim, and reveals that the entire debate rests on two foundational pillars — the two possible explanations for darkness. Let's read the passage with these questions in mind.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Pay close attention to the two questions the author asks: about the cause of mixing and about its permanence.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two opposites and the problem
Identify what the two opposites are (light and darkness) and why the author calls them 'mutually opposing in essence and nature.' Notice the rhetorical question: 'so how did they mix?'
The author assumes you know the Dualist claim that the world results from this mixture.
3
Understand the two pillars
The passage ends by saying the issue revolves around establishing two pillars. These pillars are the two possible views on darkness: either it is created (حَدَث) or eternal (قَدَم). The author will refute both.
Do not confuse the pillars with light and darkness themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطبعا وفعلا وحيزا وهما متنافران ذاتا وطبيعةً، فكيف امتزجا؟ وما الموجب لاجتماعهما حتى حصل الامتزاج، وحصل بحصول الامتزاج صور هذا العالم؟ ثم هل يبقى هذا الامتزاج أبد الدهر ويلزم عليهم كون أجزاء النور معذبة أبد الآبدين، أو تتخلص يوماً ما فما الموجب للخلاص؟ فصار مدار المسألة معهم على تقرير هذين الركنين.
And in nature, action, and locus, they are mutually opposing in essence and nature, so how did they mix? And what necessitated their coming together such that mixing occurred, and by the occurrence of mixing the forms of this world came about? Then does this mixing remain forever, necessitating that parts of light are punished eternally, or do they separate one day, and what necessitates the separation? So the pivot of the issue with them came down to establishing these two pillars.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage sets up the problem with the Dualist (Manichaean) claim that the world results from the mixture of two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). The author first notes that light and darkness are opposites in essence and nature, so their mixing is problematic. He then poses two necessary questions: (1) What caused them to come together to produce the world? (2) Does the mixture last forever (implying that parts of light are eternally punished) or does it separate at some point, and if so, what causes the separation? The passage concludes by stating that the entire discussion with the Dualists reduces to establishing two pillars (the two views on the origin of darkness: either it is created or eternal). This frames the refutation that follows.

Refutation of Darkness from a Bad Thought in Light
Refutation of dualist claim about darkness originating from bad thought.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Shahrastani refutes the dualist claim that darkness originated from an evil thought in light by exposing an internal contradiction.

Core Idea
Evil cannot arise from pure good without contradiction.

The dualists argued that light, being pure good, could not directly produce darkness; instead, they claimed a bad thought arose in light, which then brought forth darkness. Al-Shahrastani exposes the flaw in this reasoning by showing that whether the thought arises by itself or from light, the dualists are forced to trace all evil back to light itself. This lesson presents his crisp refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm, then read the translation. Notice the dualist claim and the refutation's structure.
The refutation proceeds by examining two possibilities for the origin of the bad thought.
2
Identify the dualist claim
Find the sentence describing the dualist view: light thought an evil thought, and from it darkness arose. Understand their attempt to shield light from evil.
3
Follow the refutation's logic
The author presents two possibilities: the thought occurred by itself or by light. Trace each consequence and see why both lead to a contradiction for the dualists.
The key insight: either way, light becomes responsible for evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالت طائفة منهم : إن النور فكر في نفسه فكرة ردية فحدث منها الظلام متشبئا ببعض أجزاء النور، وهذا قول من قال بحدوث الظلام. فيقال لهم : إذا كان النور خيراً لا شر فيه بوجه ما ، فما الموجب لحدوث الفكرة الردية؟ فإن حدثت بنفسها فهلا حدث الظلام بنفسه من غير أن ينسب إليه، وإن حدث بالنور فالنور كيف أحدث أصل الشر ومنبع الفساد؟ فإنه إن كان كل فساد في العالم إنما انتسب إلى الظلام والظلام انتسب إلى الفكرة كانت الفكرة مبدأ الشر والفساد. ومن العجب أنهم اعتذروا حتى لم ينسبوا شرا جزئيا إلى النور في الحوادث، ولزمهم أن ينسبوا كل الشر وأصل الفساد إليه.
A group among them said: Light thought an evil thought in itself, and from it darkness arose, attaching itself to some parts of light. This is the statement of those who say darkness is originated. So it is said to them: If light is good with no evil in it in any respect, what necessitated the occurrence of the evil thought? If it occurred by itself, then why did darkness not occur by itself without being attributed to it? And if it occurred by light, then how did light originate the source of evil and the fountain of corruption? For if all corruption in the world is attributed to darkness, and darkness is attributed to the thought, then the thought is the beginning of evil and corruption. And it is amazing that they excused themselves so that they did not attribute any partial evil to light in events, yet they were forced to attribute all evil and the source of corruption to it.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage refutes the first dualist position that darkness originated from a bad thought in light. The author presents their claim and then objects: if light is absolutely good, what caused the bad thought? Two possibilities are examined: (1) The thought occurred by itself — but then darkness could have occurred by itself without involving light. (2) The thought occurred by light itself — but then light, which is supposed to be pure good, becomes the origin of evil. The author forces the consequence: since all evil in the world traces back to darkness, and darkness traces back to the thought, the thought itself is the ultimate source of evil. Thus, the dualists who tried to avoid attributing any evil to light end up attributing all evil to light through this chain. The refutation exposes an internal contradiction in their position.

Key Terms
فكرة ردية
حدوث الظلام
الشر
الفساد
النور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualists can avoid attributing evil to light by interposing a bad thought.
Correction: Al-Shahrastani shows that this merely shifts the origin of evil back to light, because either the thought arises from light or independently; if independently, darkness could arise without light; if from light, light becomes the source of all evil.

Checkpoint
What consequence does the author draw if the evil thought occurred by light itself?
A) Light remains entirely good
B) Light becomes the source of all evil and corruption
C) Darkness is independent of light
D) The thought is not really evil

Key Takeaway
The dualist attempt to protect light's purity fails because the bad thought inevitably traces back to light, making light the origin of all evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage shows that even a single evil thought cannot arise from pure good. Examine your own heart: do you ever justify your bad thoughts as 'just thoughts' disconnected from your actions? Can you imagine a thought arising in you that is not already an exposure of your inner state? This lesson forces you to take responsibility for the origin of your evil impulses. Will you trace them back to yourself instead of blaming your environment or your history?
?
The dualists tried to protect light by blaming darkness on an intermediate evil thought. Where in your life do you create an intermediate excuse between your own goodness and your failures? Name one area where you say 'I am good, but circumstances made me do that.' This lesson says no such buffer exists. What will you do about that?
?
If every corruption traces back to a single thought, what does that say about the thoughts you allow to linger? This passage is not just a 1,000-year-old refutation of a dead heresy—it is a mirror. What thought are you holding right now that, if left unchecked, becomes the source of darkness in your life? Confess it silently and resolve to abandon it.

First Argument: Opposites Cannot Mix Without a Subduer
First rational argument against eternal darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why two extremely opposite things cannot mix by their own essences without an external subduer.

Core Idea
Opposites cannot unite by themselves; a subduer is necessary.

The first argument against the eternity of darkness begins with a basic rational principle: two things that are extremely opposite in nature cannot mix unless something external forces them to. If they could mix by themselves, their essential opposition would be destroyed. This argument sets the stage for the broader refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the argument. Then read the translation.
Notice the logical structure: condition → impossibility → contradiction.
2
Identify the key terms
Find the terms 'متنافر' (opposite) and 'قاسر' (subduer). Understand their role in the argument.
3
Parse the logical flow
The passage says: if two opposites mixed by themselves, their opposition would vanish. But they are essentially opposite, so they cannot unite. Therefore mixing requires an external subduer.
This leads to a contradiction if they mix without a subduer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال بقدم الظلام، فالرد عليه أن العقل يقضي ضرورة أن شيئين متنافرين غاية التنافر طبعا لا يمتزجان إلا بقاسر، فإنهما لو امتزجا بذاتيهما تبطل تنافرهما بذاتيهما، وما هو متنافر ذاتا لا يجوز أن يجتمع ذاتا، فالذات الواحدة لا توجب اجتماعًا وافتراقا، وذلك يقتضي ألا يحصل وجود ما وقد حصل فهو خلف. ونقول أيضاً : الظلام لا يخلو إما أن يكون موجودًا حقيقة أو لم يكن، فإن كان وجوده وجودًا حقيقيًّا فقد ساوى النور في الوجود وبطل الامتياز عنه من كل وجه، وكذلك إن ساواه في القدم والوحدة، ثم الوجود من حيث هو وجود خير لا محالة فلم يكن الظلام شراً، وإن لم يكن موجوداً حقيقة فما ليس بموجود حقيقة كيف يكون قديما ؟ وكيف ينافي ضده؟ وكيف يحصل منه امتزاج؟ وكيف يحصل من امتزاجه وجود العالم؟ ونقول أيضا : عندكم وجود خير من شر، ووجود شر من خير لا يتصور. ومن قال بحدوث الظلام فقد لزمه حدوث شر من خير، ثم حدوث العالم من الامتزاج، أوذلك حدوث خير من شر. ومن قال بقدمه فقد لزمه احصول العالم من الامتزاج، والامتزاج إن كان خيرًا فهو حصول خير من شر، وإن كان شراً فهو حصول شر من خير، ثم لو كان الامتزاج خيرًا أوجب أن يكون الخلاص شراً ؛ لأنه ضده، ولو كان شرا فالخلاص خير، وعلى أي وجه قدر فلا بد من حصول خير من شر، وحصول شر من خير ونقول أيضا : العقل بالضرورة يقضي بأن امتزاج جوهرين بسيطين لا يقتضي إلا طبيعةً واحدة، ونحن نترى مختلفات في العالم اختلافا في النوع والشخص والحقيقة والصورة على طبائع مختلفة وأعراض متضادة، وهذه الاختلافات تستحيل أن تحصل من امتزاج أمرين بسيطين فقط، فإنهما لا يوجبان الأمور على خلاف ذاتيهما
And whoever says that darkness is eternal, the refutation against him is that reason necessarily judges that two things extremely opposite in nature do not mix except with a subduer. For if they mixed by their essences, their mutual opposition by their essences would be nullified. And what is essentially opposite cannot essentially unite. So a single essence does not necessitate both conjunction and separation. And that necessitates that a certain existence should not occur, but it has occurred, so it is a contradiction. And we also say: Darkness is either truly existent or not. If its existence is true existence, then it equals light in existence and distinction from it is nullified in every respect, and likewise if it equals it in eternity and unity. Then existence qua existence is good necessarily, so darkness would not be evil. And if it is not truly existent, then what is not truly existent how can it be eternal? How can it oppose its opposite? How can mixing come from it? And how can the existence of the world come from its mixing? And we also say: According to you, occurrence of good from evil and occurrence of evil from good are inconceivable. And whoever says darkness is originated is forced to hold that evil occurs from good, then the world occurs from mixing, or that good occurs from evil. And whoever says it is eternal is forced to hold that the world occurs from mixing. And if the mixing is good, then it is the occurrence of good from evil; and if it is evil, then it is the occurrence of evil from good. Then if mixing were good, it would necessitate that separation is evil because it is its opposite; and if it were evil, then separation is good. And in whatever way it is estimated, it is inevitable that good occurs from evil and evil occurs from good. And we also say: Reason necessarily judges that the mixing of two simple substances does not necessitate except one nature. Yet we see many differences in the world—difference in kind, individual, essence, and form—upon different natures and opposite accidents. These differences are impossible to arise from the mixing of only two simple things, for they do not produce things contrary to their own essences.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage refutes the second dualist position that darkness is eternal. The author presents multiple arguments in sequence. First argument: Reason dictates that two extremely opposite things cannot mix without an external subduer (قاسر). If they mixed by their own essences, their essential opposition would be nullified, which is absurd. Also, since opposites cannot unite in essence, a single essence cannot cause both conjunction and separation; therefore the mixture's existence would be impossible, yet it exists, so it is contradictory. Second argument: Darkness must either be truly existent or not. If truly existent, it equals light in existence, and since existence is good, darkness would be good, not evil. Moreover, if it equals light in eternity and unity, all distinction vanishes. If it is not truly existent, it cannot be eternal, cannot oppose its opposite, and cannot produce mixing or the world. Third argument: The dualists accept that good cannot come from evil and evil cannot come from good. But both of their views (origination and eternity of darkness) lead to such impossible consequences. If darkness is originated, then evil (darkness) comes from good (light's thought), and from mixing, the world arises—so either evil from good or good from evil. If darkness is eternal, the world arises from mixing, and mixing itself is either good or evil; either way, good from evil or evil from good follows. Also, the final outcome (separation from mixture) would then be opposite to the mixture, perpetuating the absurdity. Fourth argument: The mixing of two simple substances yields only one nature, but the world contains many different kinds, individuals, essences, forms, natures, and opposite accidents. These cannot arise from just two simple things, because simple things do not produce effects contrary to their own essences. Thus, the dualist account of the world's diversity is impossible.

Key Terms
متنافر
قاسر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that opposites can mix naturally without any external cause.
Correction: The argument shows that essential opposites cannot unite by themselves; a subduer is necessary, otherwise their essence would contradict itself.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, why can't two extremely opposite things mix by themselves?
A) Because they are too different
B) Because mixing would nullify their essential opposition
C) Because they are both eternal
D) Because they are made of the same substance

Key Takeaway
The first argument establishes that extreme opposites cannot mix without an external subduer, refuting the independent eternity of darkness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in one God, but do you ever act as if good and evil are equally powerful? How does this argument force you to see that evil cannot be independent? What would change in your daily life if you truly internalized that Allah is the sole subduer of all opposites?
?
When you face moral darkness, do you feel overwhelmed by its apparent power? This argument shows that darkness cannot even exist without a subduer. How does that change your response to sin and hardship?
?
Are you willing to submit to Allah as the Qāhir (Subduer) in every area of your life, even those where you feel darkness is in control? What step will you take today to acknowledge His sole power over opposites?

Second Argument: Darkness as Truly Existent or Not
Dilemma argument on existence of darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why darkness cannot be eternal whether it is truly existent or not, and how the notion of existence entails goodness.

Core Idea
If darkness is truly existent, it would be good; if not, it cannot be eternal or effective.

The second argument examines two possibilities: either darkness is truly existent or it is not. If it is truly existent, it equals light in existence, and since existence as such is good, darkness would be good, contradicting its nature as evil. If it is not truly existent, it cannot be eternal, cannot oppose light, and cannot produce mixing or the world. This dilemma forces the dualist into a contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the two cases.
Look for the phrase 'لا يخلو إما أن يكون' which introduces the division.
2
Analyze the first case
If darkness is truly existent, it equals light in existence. Since existence is good, darkness would be good, not evil.
This also nullifies distinction from light in eternity and unity.
3
Analyze the second case
If darkness is not truly existent, it cannot be eternal, cannot oppose, and cannot produce mixing or the world.
This shows the absurdity of the dualist position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال بقدم الظلام، فالرد عليه أن العقل يقضي ضرورة أن شيئين متنافرين غاية التنافر طبعا لا يمتزجان إلا بقاسر، فإنهما لو امتزجا بذاتيهما تبطل تنافرهما بذاتيهما، وما هو متنافر ذاتا لا يجوز أن يجتمع ذاتا، فالذات الواحدة لا توجب اجتماعًا وافتراقا، وذلك يقتضي ألا يحصل وجود ما وقد حصل فهو خلف. ونقول أيضاً : الظلام لا يخلو إما أن يكون موجودًا حقيقة أو لم يكن، فإن كان وجوده وجودًا حقيقيًّا فقد ساوى النور في الوجود وبطل الامتياز عنه من كل وجه، وكذلك إن ساواه في القدم والوحدة، ثم الوجود من حيث هو وجود خير لا محالة فلم يكن الظلام شراً، وإن لم يكن موجوداً حقيقة فما ليس بموجود حقيقة كيف يكون قديما ؟ وكيف ينافي ضده؟ وكيف يحصل منه امتزاج؟ وكيف يحصل من امتزاجه وجود العالم؟ ونقول أيضا : عندكم وجود خير من شر، ووجود شر من خير لا يتصور. ومن قال بحدوث الظلام فقد لزمه حدوث شر من خير، ثم حدوث العالم من الامتزاج، أوذلك حدوث خير من شر. ومن قال بقدمه فقد لزمه احصول العالم من الامتزاج، والامتزاج إن كان خيرًا فهو حصول خير من شر، وإن كان شراً فهو حصول شر من خير، ثم لو كان الامتزاج خيرًا أوجب أن يكون الخلاص شراً ؛ لأنه ضده، ولو كان شرا فالخلاص خير، وعلى أي وجه قدر فلا بد من حصول خير من شر، وحصول شر من خير ونقول أيضا : العقل بالضرورة يقضي بأن امتزاج جوهرين بسيطين لا يقتضي إلا طبيعةً واحدة، ونحن نترى مختلفات في العالم اختلافا في النوع والشخص والحقيقة والصورة على طبائع مختلفة وأعراض متضادة، وهذه الاختلافات تستحيل أن تحصل من امتزاج أمرين بسيطين فقط، فإنهما لا يوجبان الأمور على خلاف ذاتيهما
And whoever says that darkness is eternal, the refutation against him is that reason necessarily judges that two things extremely opposite in nature do not mix except with a subduer. For if they mixed by their essences, their mutual opposition by their essences would be nullified. And what is essentially opposite cannot essentially unite. So a single essence does not necessitate both conjunction and separation. And that necessitates that a certain existence should not occur, but it has occurred, so it is a contradiction. And we also say: Darkness is either truly existent or not. If its existence is true existence, then it equals light in existence and distinction from it is nullified in every respect, and likewise if it equals it in eternity and unity. Then existence qua existence is good necessarily, so darkness would not be evil. And if it is not truly existent, then what is not truly existent how can it be eternal? How can it oppose its opposite? How can mixing come from it? And how can the existence of the world come from its mixing? And we also say: According to you, occurrence of good from evil and occurrence of evil from good are inconceivable. And whoever says darkness is originated is forced to hold that evil occurs from good, then the world occurs from mixing, or that good occurs from evil. And whoever says it is eternal is forced to hold that the world occurs from mixing. And if the mixing is good, then it is the occurrence of good from evil; and if it is evil, then it is the occurrence of evil from good. Then if mixing were good, it would necessitate that separation is evil because it is its opposite; and if it were evil, then separation is good. And in whatever way it is estimated, it is inevitable that good occurs from evil and evil occurs from good. And we also say: Reason necessarily judges that the mixing of two simple substances does not necessitate except one nature. Yet we see many differences in the world—difference in kind, individual, essence, and form—upon different natures and opposite accidents. These differences are impossible to arise from the mixing of only two simple things, for they do not produce things contrary to their own essences.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage refutes the second dualist position that darkness is eternal. The author presents multiple arguments in sequence. First argument: Reason dictates that two extremely opposite things cannot mix without an external subduer (قاسر). If they mixed by their own essences, their essential opposition would be nullified, which is absurd. Also, since opposites cannot unite in essence, a single essence cannot cause both conjunction and separation; therefore the mixture's existence would be impossible, yet it exists, so it is contradictory. Second argument: Darkness must either be truly existent or not. If truly existent, it equals light in existence, and since existence is good, darkness would be good, not evil. Moreover, if it equals light in eternity and unity, all distinction vanishes. If it is not truly existent, it cannot be eternal, cannot oppose its opposite, and cannot produce mixing or the world. Third argument: The dualists accept that good cannot come from evil and evil cannot come from good. But both of their views (origination and eternity of darkness) lead to such impossible consequences. If darkness is originated, then evil (darkness) comes from good (light's thought), and from mixing, the world arises—so either evil from good or good from evil. If darkness is eternal, the world arises from mixing, and mixing itself is either good or evil; either way, good from evil or evil from good follows. Also, the final outcome (separation from mixture) would then be opposite to the mixture, perpetuating the absurdity. Fourth argument: The mixing of two simple substances yields only one nature, but the world contains many different kinds, individuals, essences, forms, natures, and opposite accidents. These cannot arise from just two simple things, because simple things do not produce effects contrary to their own essences. Thus, the dualist account of the world's diversity is impossible.

Key Terms
وجود حقيقي
خير
شر
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think darkness can be eternal yet non-existent, or existent yet evil.
Correction: The argument shows that true existence entails goodness, and non-existence cannot have attributes like eternity or causal power.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, if darkness is truly existent, what follows?
A) It would be inferior to light
B) It would be evil because it is dark
C) It would be good because existence is good
D) It would be temporary

Key Takeaway
The second argument shows that darkness cannot be eternal, because true existence entails goodness and non-existence lacks eternity and causal power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute reality to evils in your life as if they have an existence of their own, forgetting that only good is truly real and lasting? How would this argument change your perspective on a current struggle?
?
When you face darkness (ignorance, sin, despair), do you treat it as a powerful independent force? How can remembering that non-existence cannot cause anything empower you to turn toward the Light?
?
If existence itself is good, then what does your preoccupation with non-existent fears or past wrongs reveal about your heart's orientation? Will you deliberately redirect your attention today to what truly exists and is good?

Third Argument: Inevitable Good-from-Evil Consequences
Argument from dualist's own principles on good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dualist view leads to the absurdity that good can come from evil and evil from good.

Core Idea
Both dualist views force good to come from evil and evil from good, which is impossible.

The third argument targets the dualist principle that good cannot come from evil and vice versa. The author shows that whether darkness is originated or eternal, the dualist is forced into the very consequence they deny. If darkness is originated, then evil (darkness) comes from good (light's thought), and the world from mixing involves either good from evil or evil from good. Similarly, if darkness is eternal, the mixing itself is either good or evil, but either way the result is an impossible inversion of values.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the conditional structure.
Notice the phrases 'فقد لزمه' and 'فقد لزمه'.
2
Consider the first scenario
If darkness is originated, then evil comes from good (since light's thought is good), and the world arises from mixing—either evil from good or good from evil.
3
Consider the second scenario
If darkness is eternal, the mixing is either good or evil, leading again to good from evil or evil from good.
Also explore the implications for separation as opposite of mixing.

?
